  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6bfe3f98-adec-4a9b-b2ca-308c5f82106a'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2552517859534187310">The Hematoi descend from the unions of gods and mortals, and the children of two Hematoi pure bloods have godlike powers. Children of Hematoi and mortals--well, not so much. Half-bloods only have two options: become trained Sentinels who hunt and kill daimons or become servants in the homes of the pures.<br/><br/>Seventeen-year-old Alexandria would rather risk her life fighting than</span>
  <span id="freeText2552517859534187310" style="display:none">The Hematoi descend from the unions of gods and mortals, and the children of two Hematoi pure bloods have godlike powers. Children of Hematoi and mortals--well, not so much. Half-bloods only have two options: become trained Sentinels who hunt and kill daimons or become servants in the homes of the pures.<br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Alexandria would rather risk her life fighting than waste it scrubbing toilets, but she may end up slumming it anyway. There are several rules that students at the Covenant must follow. Alex has problems with them all, but especially rule #1:Relationships between pures and halfs are forbidden. Unfortunately, she's crushing hard on the totally hot pure-blood Aiden. But falling for Aiden isn't her biggest problem--staying alive long enough to graduate the Covenant and become a Sentinel is.<br /><br />If she fails in her duty, she faces a future worse than death or slavery: being turned into a daimon, and being hunted by Aiden. And that would kind of suck.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2552517859534187310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/159178-is-it-anything-like-the-lux-series">Is it anything like the Lux series ?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_159178'><a id="like_count_community_question_159178" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/159178?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">11 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F9680718-half-blood">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/159178-is-it-anything-like-the-lux-series">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/159178-is-it-anything-like-the-lux-series">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/20487928-jessica"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1373947322i/20487928._UY100_CR34,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/20487928-jessica">Jessica</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Are you familiar with Richelle Mead's Vampire Academy? If so, then there is a similar sense of plot to Armentrout's Covenant series. This series is st<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Are you familiar with Richelle Mead's Vampire Academy? If so, then there is a similar sense of plot to Armentrout's Covenant series. This series is still unique in its own, however, and an awesome read. (If you do decide to read the books, then you'll know what I mean when I say that the series is worth it just for Aiden and Seth). If you haven't read the Vampire Academy series, then I highly recommend you read the Covenant series. It is based on Greek mythology and actually makes for a very entertaining read.<br /><br />As for the Lux series, I can see some parallels. The plot and basis of the two series are complete and polar opposites, but the characters' traits are distinctly similar. Armentrout includes a lot of snark and hilarity in the Covenant series (which actually makes it all the more interesting to read...not that the books are bad as a standalone, but her amazing sense of humor shows in her writing) and Aiden is striking similar to Daemon in the Lux series. Both men are fiercely protective, somewhat standoffish at times, but are completely and utterly willing to die for the woman that they love. Oh, and they're also both unbelievably sexy. ;)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4646529639631231522">SPOILER ALERT **THERE ARE SPOILERS FOR BOTH VAMPIRE ACADEMY (the whole series) AND HALF BLOOD BELOW***<br/><br/>Similarities Between Half-Blood and Vampire Academy<br/><br/> <b>EVERY. SINGLE. THING.</b><br/><br/>*CAUTION* if you're looking for originality this is not the book for you. <br/><br/>It's like the author just took Vampire Academy and changed all the names. The only character missing from this story is <s>Lissa</s>. Read below for details<br/><br/><b>*EDIT*</b> Apparently Lissa is in this book as well. You know the connection that Rose and Lisa have that </span>
  <span id="freeText4646529639631231522" style="display:none">SPOILER ALERT **THERE ARE SPOILERS FOR BOTH VAMPIRE ACADEMY (the whole series) AND HALF BLOOD BELOW***<br /><br />Similarities Between Half-Blood and Vampire Academy<br /><br /> <b>EVERY. SINGLE. THING.</b><br /><br />*CAUTION* if you're looking for originality this is not the book for you. <br /><br />It's like the author just took Vampire Academy and changed all the names. The only character missing from this story is <s>Lissa</s>. Read below for details<br /><br /><b>*EDIT*</b> Apparently Lissa is in this book as well. You know the connection that Rose and Lisa have that allows them to experience each other's feelings and hear thoughts? It's the same as the connection between Alex and Seth in Half-Blood. So Seth is actually playing the part of Lissa. :/ <br /><br /><b>Here's our "cast":</b><br /><br />Alex AKA Rose Hathaway<br /><br />Aidan AKA Dimitri<br /><br />Deacon/Seth AKA Adrian<br />* Deacon (HB) and Adrian (VA) both have drinking problems* <br /><br />Caleb AKA Mason<br /><br />Lea AKA Mia ....gosh their names even rhyme -__- <br />In the Vampire Academy Mia's mother dies due to Strigoi attacks, in Half Blood Lea's parent dies due to Daimon attacks. They are also both the mean-girl antagonist of the story who turn out not to hate each other towards the end. Seriously? Could this be even more obvious that this is a rip-off without stealing such a minuscule detail from the story? <br /><br /><br /><b>Terms:</b><br /><br />HALF-BLOOD - Basically the same thing as DHAMPIRS<br /><br />PURE-BLOOD - Basically the same thing as MOROI (notice that they both "coincidently" have the same ability to control the elements and not the Half-bloods/dhampirs)<br /><br />DAIMONS - Basically the SAME thing as STRIGOI<br /><br /><br /><b>Other similarities:</b> <br /><br />In Vampire Academy Rose escapes from the Academy/ school for vampires with Lisa<br />In Half-Blood Alex escapes the academy with her mother<br /><br />In Vampire Academy Rose goes to visit Dimitri at his house and they almost go all the way (In that scene Dimitri talks in Russian)<br />In Half-Blood Alex goes to Aidan's cabin and they almost go all the way (In that scene Aiden talks in Greek)<br /><br /><br />In Vampire Academy Rose is distraught when Dimitri gets turned into a Strigoi<br />In Half-Blood Alex is distraught when her mother turns into a Diamon<br /><br /><br />The structures of the school and the society. THE EXACT SAME THING.<br />In VA there are Dhampir and Moroi vampires - Dhampir = half-blooded, Morio- pure blooded<br />Dhampirs in VA are meant to protect and cater to the needs of Moroi<br />In Halfs-Blood, Halfs are expected to cater to the needs of PURES. Halfs are considered below the pures. Same for VA. <br /><br />In Half-Blood HALFS train in combat to Protect people from Diamons<br />In Vampire Academy DHAMPIRS train in Combat to protect people from Strigoi. <br /><br />The similarities are endless. <b>Bottom line</b>--this story was a complete rip-off of VA. Coincidence? I think not. The story follows the plot way too closely. It's impossible not to miss. <br /><br />Good news? I loved the author's voice/style and Alex's characters. Why? Because they're the only thing about this story that's even remotely ORIGINAL. I have a strong dislike for books that are rip-offs of other books (rip-off isn't even the correct word for this book--more like half-stolen) but I enjoyed the story nonetheless--mostly because I missed VA and this story was basically a re-write of it. Towards the end the author surprises us by using some of her own ideas. I hope she continues with that in the next book.<br /><br />UPDATE: 11/13/11<br /><br />EX. OF SIMILAR DIALOGUE: <br />“You will lose what you value most, so treasure it while you can.” <br />― Richelle Mead, Shadow Kiss <br /><br />-__- Doesn't the witch lady from Half-Blood say the EXACT SAME THING? I didn't even notice this till today but seriously I'm speechless? There's also A LOT more copies of dialogue during the Alex/Rose and Dimitri/Aiden moments.<br /><br /><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br /><br />I try to never compare books to each other. I actually find it kind of annoying. But this book isn't just similar, it's been copied to the point where I got <i>confused</i> over whether I was reading Half-Blood or Vampire Academy. Whole plots/characters/scenes/ and dialogue have been copied. And <b>no</b> I will not convince myself to give this author credit for stealing from VA just because she wrote a novel. <br /><br /><b>Let me explain this in a different situation:</b> A person steals a college essay off the internet and changes the names, locations, and switches the words around, but at it's core it's somebody else's words--somebody else's hard work. That person gets into their top college, in big part to "their" gut-wrenching essay. That person does not give credit to the original essay writer and is taking all the congratulations for getting into this college that's super tough to get into. Would YOU think that was okay to do??? That is why I cannot reward plagiarism, even though I enjoyed reading Half-Blood. It's not fair, it's unprofessional, and it's an insult to the person she stole from. I mean, she's making profit from someone else's work, without their consent. NOT cool at all, whatsoever. You want to be proud of something that you created, not guilt-ridden. <br /><br />- - - - - - -<br /><br />So I went on to read the second book, hoping the rumors were true that the it was completely vampire-academy-less. So <b>not</b> true! But I admit that she did try harder to use original ideas than she did in the first book. Here's my review of PURE:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306118648">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4646529639631231522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208428483" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208428483?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208428483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15747321331884517570"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Surely this book is illegal. I mean, someone once tried to sue <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling' title='J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.K. Rowling</a> because their book included a kind of wizard sport tournament similar to the one found in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire' title='Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire by J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a>, they claimed she had stolen the idea from them... and this small matter takes up such a minuscule percentage of the novel! Not to mention the fact that no one I knew had ever heard of the guy's novel before...<br/><br/>Now, pretty much everyone I speak to has heard of - if not read - the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_' title='Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vampire Academ</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15747321331884517570" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Surely this book is illegal. I mean, someone once tried to sue <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a> because their book included a kind of wizard sport tournament similar to the one found in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a>, they claimed she had stolen the idea from them... and this small matter takes up such a minuscule percentage of the novel! Not to mention the fact that no one I knew had ever heard of the guy's novel before...<br><br>Now, pretty much everyone I speak to has heard of - if not read - the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> series. The first two thirds of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9680718.Half_Blood__Covenant___1_" title="Half-Blood (Covenant, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Half-Blood</a> is exactly the same as the first in the VA series, I'm not even exaggerating. There are some scenes where if you changed "Alex" to "Rose" and "Aiden" to "Dimitri" then you would have a difficult time guessing which book is which. In each novel, the protagonist has been away from their centre of training (St Vladimir's and The Covenant) for a long period of time. When they return, they are admitted for a trial period in which they must attend training by professional (and super sexy) hunters. In the training rooms, they fight the older and forbidden pros and get their arses handed to them repeatedly... then slowly they get better, stronger, and things start to get just a little too hot and sweaty between them and their trainers.<br><br>Oh, and another in-your-face similarity? There are pures and half-bloods, the former look down on the latter, pures would never stoop so low as to start a relationship with a half-blood, etc, etc. Alex, like Rose, is a half-blood. The only big difference is that Aiden, unlike Dimitri, is a pure. So the relationship in this novel is even more forbidden than the one in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a>. But I was just astounded by how many characters mirrored the ones in VA, this wasn't an accident, it simply couldn't be.<br><br>Two stars on goodreads means "it was ok" and, trust me, this very nearly got one star because plagiarism is never ok. But there was a big improvement in the last third that gave me the feeling that the second book in this series - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9761771.Pure__Covenant___2_" title="Pure (Covenant, #2) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Pure</a> - would leave the VA books alone and show some originality. Things started to branch off from the obviously stolen idea and take their own shape; like the introduction of Apollyon (a half-blood who is granted super powers in order to keep pures in check, but only one can exist at any given time) and some other interesting discoveries that I can't talk about without giving away huge spoilers.<br><br>Even though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9680718.Half_Blood__Covenant___1_" title="Half-Blood (Covenant, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Half-Blood</a> is a well-written, dark and sexy novel, I couldn't help but be turned off when I discovered that the author had taken someone else's idea. Perhaps I'd have felt differently if I hadn't just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> in 2011? I don't know, but I'm not particularly interested in reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9761771.Pure__Covenant___2_" title="Pure (Covenant, #2) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Pure</a> right now. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15747321331884517570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1127319682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127319682" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127319682?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Katerina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2389682-amanda">Amanda</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127319682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7124087731635922612"><b>I'm in love with Aiden St. Delphi.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454841490ra/18019689.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Of course that's not a big surprise, since he's the <b>reincarnation</b> of one of my first and eternal book crushes, <b>Dimitri Belikov</b>, but still it's a reason to smile (well, not for my mother, she weeps every time I fall for another fictional character instead of producing grand-children).<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You will kill the ones you love. It is in your blood, in your fate. So the gods have spoken it and so the gods have come to foresee it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>There is a secret society, one us</span>
  <span id="freeText7124087731635922612" style="display:none"><b>I'm in love with Aiden St. Delphi.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454841490ra/18019689.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course that's not a big surprise, since he's the <b>reincarnation</b> of one of my first and eternal book crushes, <b>Dimitri Belikov</b>, but still it's a reason to smile (well, not for my mother, she weeps every time I fall for another fictional character instead of producing grand-children).<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You will kill the ones you love. It is in your blood, in your fate. So the gods have spoken it and so the gods have come to foresee it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There is a secret society, one us mortals are not aware of. Once upon a time, the horny greek gods mated with humans, and thus the Hematoi (or Pure-Bloods) <s>Moroi</s> were born. Due to their divine heritage, they are extremely fast and strong (and beautiful), and they can wield elemental magic. Their lesser halfs are the Half-Bloods <s>Dhampirs</s>. They can't control the elements, but they're equally strong. Not particularly respected though. A Half-Blood will either become a servant, or will get the proper training to guard the Pure-Bloods, and the best of them, they can become Sentinels. Daimon hunters. Which brings us to the third kind of supernatural, gods-descended beings. Daimons <s>Strigoi</s> are the Pures that switched to the dark side, and feed on Pures. Our main heroine is Alexandria Andros (why her last name is a greek island is beyond me), who fled the Covenant with her mother, only to be dragged back after her mother's death. In order to graduate, she must train with my aforementioned love Aiden, a badass Pure, and try to survive the Pures' politics, daimon attacks, shocking revelations about her powers and her ever-growing yearning for Aiden. Because relationships between Pures and Halfs are strictly forbidden.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Okay. I’m ready to move onto something else, like practicing with knives or defense against the dark arts. Cool things.”<br>“Did you just quote Harry Potter?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>As you can tell, there are many similarities with <b>Vampire Academy</b>. That's not a bad thing in my agenda, it's just that due to this resemblance the whole story lost the element of surprise for me. I knew exactly what was going to happen, when and where and how. But setting this aside, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9680718.Half_Blood__Covenant___1_" title="Half-Blood (Covenant, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Half-Blood</a> <b>was delicious</b>. When it comes to <b>action, rich mythology, feisty characters and scorching tension</b>, you know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> can not disappoint. <b>Fast-paced, snarky, funny and equally heart-breaking</b>, Alex's story hooked you from the start, from that very first show-down with daimons to the melancholic and beautiful last chapter. There was just one problem.<br>Alex.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483715349ra/21642485.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am the President of the <b>Alex-Andros-Sucks</b> club. The position of the Vice President is still up for grabs. I had such a hard time liking her, since her <b>lack of self-control</b> and discipline, her total disregard for the rules, <b>her selfish, reckless and impulsive attitude</b> that kept endangering not only her, but also the people close to her, were too much for me. I know that most YA heroines are like this but, believe me when I say it, she is worse. So much worse.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475859895ra/20776107.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On the bright side, Rose Hathaway really grew up throughout Vampire Academy, so I'm not losing hope yet. Even though Alex is the reason I almost gave <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9680718.Half_Blood__Covenant___1_" title="Half-Blood (Covenant, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Half-Blood</a> 3 stars, it is Aiden that <b>deserves all the stars in the sky</b>. He's so caring, fierce and sweet that he makes your heart melt. The chemistry between Alex and Aiden is simply <b>sizzling</b>, their scenes are both <b>tender and toe-curling</b>, and swooning is inevitable.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Then he leaned forward and rested his cheek against mine. Hot tingles spread through me as his lips moved against my ear. "You should tell me to stop." <br>I didn't say a word.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But alas, I can sense a love triangle coming, and somebody will end up crying. Probably me. The good thing is, there is a reason behind it. It won't be thrown for drama purposes only, but it serves the plot, so I'm going pretend it won't bother me a lot.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Need covers itself with love, but need… need is never love. Always beware of the one who needs you. There is always a want behind a need, you see.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Despite its flaws, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9680718.Half_Blood__Covenant___1_" title="Half-Blood (Covenant, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Half-Blood</a> is an <b>addictive ride</b> I absolutely recommend to every <b>paranormal/forbidden romance/greek mythology</b> lover!<br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/katerina_papas/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/KaterinaPapas" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="http://booknest.eu/index.php/component/k2/item/305-halfblood" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></span>

<div id="review_145805830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145805830" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145805830?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-i-can-t-wait-to-read-in-2011">books-i-can-t-wait-to-read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=creepy-love-triangle">creepy-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=totally-saw-that-coming">totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=huge-disappointment">huge-disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=incredibly-stupid-choices">incredibly-stupid-choices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145805830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3826214028679973291">In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10860399.Daimon__Covenant___0_5_' title='Daimon (Covenant, #0.5) by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Daimon</a>, the short story prequel, Alex’s mother was killed by a group of <s>Strigoi</s> daimons, but Alex was lucky enough to escape. At the beginning of Half-Blood, she is found by <s>Dimitri</s> Aiden and other <s>Guardians</s> Sentinels and returned to the Covenant, where she hopes to continue her education. However, the dean is none too happy with her. She has lost three years of training and he thinks she shouldn’t be allowed to rejoin her classmates. Instead, he wants to give her the elixir which will turn h</span>
  <span id="freeText3826214028679973291" style="display:none">In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10860399.Daimon__Covenant___0_5_" title="Daimon (Covenant, #0.5) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Daimon</a>, the short story prequel, Alex’s mother was killed by a group of <s>Strigoi</s> daimons, but Alex was lucky enough to escape. At the beginning of Half-Blood, she is found by <s>Dimitri</s> Aiden and other <s>Guardians</s> Sentinels and returned to the Covenant, where she hopes to continue her education. However, the dean is none too happy with her. She has lost three years of training and he thinks she shouldn’t be allowed to rejoin her classmates. Instead, he wants to give her the elixir which will turn her into a mindless slave for the <s>Moroi</s> Pures. Of course, Aiden steps up and offers to train her in his free time and because of his words, Alex is given a chance to prove that she can become just as good as the others by the end of the summer. <br /><br />Relationships between Pures and Half-Bloods are strictly forbidden. Alex is a half-blood, try guessing what Aiden is! If they end up together and someone finds out, nothing will happen to Aiden because he’s a Pure, but Alex will be forced into slavery and will probably have to be a servant in her stepfather’s (who also happens to be a very powerful politician) house. <br /><br />I think this book was some sort of an experiment: how much can an author take from another author and avoid being sued for plagiarism?! Jennifer Armentrout crossed the line considerably if you ask me. It’s true that we are used to YA paranormal literature being formulaic, but that’s not what this is about. Armentrout wasn’t just following the usual formula - more than half of this book is flat-out stolen. Far too many characters and situations were just copied from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> series to Half-Blood for it to be an accident. I can't help but wonder what this woman was thinking. She had too know how obvious it'll be.<br /><br />Under normal circumstances, Half-Blood would have been a solid 4-star book for me. The characters are interesting enough, the world is well built, the plot is compelling and the writing itself isn’t half bad. But I can’t bring myself to reward Armentrout’s actions. If I do, <b>if we all do</b>, where will it end? <br /><br />There are some differences between Half-Blood and Vampire Academy, especially in the second half. But by the time I reached those parts, I was already going back and forth from depressed to angry and I just couldn’t find it within myself to care. <br /><br />Vampire Academy fans should read this out of sheer curiosity. I recommend borrowing it from the library or something because buying it means encouraging other <s>thieves</s> authors to do the same. I really don’t want to see The Panthers of Hope Falls on some shelf next year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3826214028679973291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1714102064" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1714102064" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1714102064?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12737871-half-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1714102064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10261126320262339233">Paranormal/fantasy books are not my favorite genre, but every once in a while I like to read one to change things up a bit. This one had been sitting on my TBR list for quite some time and when I saw the Audible edition on sale, I decided that it was as good a time as ever to finally give it a listen. While I'd by lying if I said that it was the kind of book that makes me fall in love with the characters and rush out to grab a copy of the next book in the series, I can't deny that I enjoyed it.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText10261126320262339233" style="display:none">Paranormal/fantasy books are not my favorite genre, but every once in a while I like to read one to change things up a bit. This one had been sitting on my TBR list for quite some time and when I saw the Audible edition on sale, I decided that it was as good a time as ever to finally give it a listen. While I'd by lying if I said that it was the kind of book that makes me fall in love with the characters and rush out to grab a copy of the next book in the series, I can't deny that I enjoyed it.<br /><br />The story centers on a seventeen year-old girl who was born into a "secret society" of sorts. She is what is called a half-blood, born of a pure-blood "Hematoi" mother and a human father. She was schooled at the Covenant, where pure-bloods and half-bloods train to be Sentinels - fighters that hunt daimons, the evil pure-bloods that feed off of other pure-bloods.<br /><br />However, before Alexandria could complete her training her mother leaves the Covenant, taking her with her. The two are on the run, hunted by the Covenant's sentinels. When they fall prey to the daimons, Alexandria's mother is killed and Alexandria is returned to the Covenant.<br /><br />Upon her return, Alexandria is given a mixed reception. Her uncle and stepfather seem to be out for her blood, wanting to relegate her to the role of a servant. She is unexpectedly championed by Aiden St. Delphi, the sentinel that is the best of the best and as good-looking as he is talented as a fighter.<br /><br />Aiden argues that Alexandria has a lot of potential as a fighter. He was impressed with the way she held her own against the daimons, even managing to kill successfully. This is a feat that is practically unheard of, especially for a half-blood that has not completed training. <br /><br />He proposes that he be allowed to personally teach Alexandria. If he can get her caught up on the training that she has missed, then she will be allowed to return to train with the others. There isn't much time and the odds are against them, but he's confident that it can be done.<br /><br />When Alexandria's uncle reluctantly agrees to Aiden's plan, the clock starts counting down. Alexandria undergoes rigorous training, growing closer to Aiden with every day. She cannot deny her attraction to him, but knows that nothing can ever come of it because unions between half-bloods and pure-bloods are strictly forbidden.<br /><br />Making matters more complicated is Alexandria's youthful, often immature, disposition. She is wild and reckless. Often, she fails to recognize the implications of her actions, acting out in dangerous ways. It is almost like she wants to be kicked out of the program, even as she denies this wholeheartedly.<br /><br />Things come to a head when Alexandria is faced with an impossible situation. Her loyalties are tested and she finds herself in more danger than she'd ever imagined. However, new facts come to light, revealing that she is far more important than anyone had ever known before.<br /><br />All things considered, this was a great book. I enjoyed it, but it was a little innocent for my tastes. It was written with a younger, teen audience in mind, so it hit it's mark for the genre. However, I require a little more steam. <br /><br />While the brewing love story between Aiden and Alexandria was tantalizing, it was more like a tease. The primary focus of the story was on the paranormal/action aspects. I needed less fight scenes and more romance. That being said, if you're looking for a paranormal/fantasy book with a lot of action, then this is a fantastic choice.<br /><br />At some point, I might continue the series, but I'm not worried about it right now. For me, personally, it just wasn't compelling enough. I don't have that anxious, impatient need to get my hands on the next one, like I do when a read a favorite. Nothing wrong with it, just not my cup of tea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10261126320262339233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2224691043049925258">unsurprisingly, the queen of YA paranormal has done it again. from aliens to angels and gargoyles, i have never not enjoyed a JLA book. and now i can add the conflict between half-blood children of gods and daimons to the list of things that entertain me. <br/><br/>there is such an innocent quality to JLAs writing. it takes me back to a simpler time when a story didnt need much to impress me - just easy writing, relatable characters, and a fun story. <br/><br/>although, i do wish this had more greek mythology prese</span>
  <span id="freeText2224691043049925258" style="display:none">unsurprisingly, the queen of YA paranormal has done it again. from aliens to angels and gargoyles, i have never not enjoyed a JLA book. and now i can add the conflict between half-blood children of gods and daimons to the list of things that entertain me. <br /><br />there is such an innocent quality to JLAs writing. it takes me back to a simpler time when a story didnt need much to impress me - just easy writing, relatable characters, and a fun story. <br /><br />although, i do wish this had more greek mythology present. for a story about pure and half bloods, the gods have no actual role in the plot at all. i think zeus is only mentioned like twice. so thats kind of a bummer. maybe they will become more involved as the series progresses?<br /><br />regardless, this is everything i love about JLAs series, so i have no doubt the other books will be just as enjoyable. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1842301757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1842301757" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1842301757?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1842301757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8212944404204484671"><b>
  <i>”The things people will do for love. All truths come down to love, do they not? One way or another, they do. See, there is a difference between love and need. Sometimes, what you feel is immediate and without rhyme or reason.” <br/>“Two people see each across a room or their skin brushes. Their souls recognize the person as their own. It doesn’t need time to figure it. The soul always knows… whether it’s right or wrong.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Team Aiden all the way. I’m decided.<br/><br/>I love everything about this world. The c</span>
  <span id="freeText8212944404204484671" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”The things people will do for love. All truths come down to love, do they not? One way or another, they do. See, there is a difference between love and need. Sometimes, what you feel is immediate and without rhyme or reason.” <br />“Two people see each across a room or their skin brushes. Their souls recognize the person as their own. It doesn’t need time to figure it. The soul always knows… whether it’s right or wrong.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Team Aiden all the way. I’m decided.<br /><br />I love everything about this world. The concept of the Greek gods in this book is great. Hematoi are the children of Gods and mortals. The children of two Hematoi are pure bloods who can control the elements. Children of a Hematoi and a mortal gives a half-blood who doesn’t have magic but has strength and the ability to see the true form a Daimon. As the blurb says, the half-bloods are considered below the pures and either become Sentinels to kill Daimons or to be pushed into servitude. <br /><br />The characters are truly amazing. The protagonist Alexandria is not who you would expect a protagonist of fantasy series with a paranormal vibe. She is light-hearted, snarky, irrational, and is driven by her emotions. Her mother’s death hardens her but watching the events of this book gradually change her is intriguing.<br />Alex had been on the run from Daimons since they invaded her house and killed her mother. Now, Alex is taken back to the Covenant to be trained as a Sentinel, which has been her dream. Three years ago, Alex’s mother took Alex and ran away from the Covenant with no reason and now to be accepted back into the Covenant and to be trained she must prove that she can catch up with everything she has missed. If Alex makes any mistakes or fails to prove her worth she will either be killed or given the Elixir which will turn her into a mindless servant. <br /><br />The plot itself is bigger than Alex proving her worth but revealing anything else would be a spoiler. As events unfold, the story moves forward in many more ways than Alex becoming a Sentinel.<br /><br />The blurb doesn’t give it away but I wanted to tell you guys that this series consists of a love triangle, which I probably gave away by the first sentence of this review. If I had known that this series had a love triangle I would probably be more hesitant to read it, and as always the love triangle frustrates me to no end but the book is still a great read. <br /><br />The plot of these books is great and the characters are amazing. The world building and the history of the world and these supernatural creatures is mind-blowing. <br />But the one thing that frustrated me is that the protagonist ignores everything the Oracle says. Yes, there is an oracle in this book but while she is considered an Oracle the protagonist doesn’t pay attention to many of the things she says till after the events occur. It is understandable that the words of the oracle weren’t interpreted, but the fact that the words were not even given any consideration is pretty irritating. Some part of what the Oracle said is not even very cryptic and could have been understood, but no Alex didn’t pay any attention to what she said.<br /><br />Putting that aside, the book was great at highlighting the relationship between the characters and revealing just as much past as the future of the characters. I look forward to the rest of the books and have a good feeling about them, but I really hope this love triangle will end soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8212944404204484671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_519852890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519852890" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519852890?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8429172-laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519852890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9298698573900614186"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif' width='500' height='245' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>You will kill the ones you love.<br/>Fate had been right about that.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Blurb: <i> The Hematoi descend from the unions of gods and mortals, and the children of two Hematoi pure bloods have godlike powers. Children of Hematoi and mortals--well, not so much. Half-bloods only have two options: become trained Sentinels who hunt and kill daimons or become servants in the homes of the pures. Seventeen-year-old Alexandria would rather risk her life fighting than waste it scrubbing toilets, but she may </i></span>
  <span id="freeText9298698573900614186" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>You will kill the ones you love.<br>Fate had been right about that.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Blurb: <i> The Hematoi descend from the unions of gods and mortals, and the children of two Hematoi pure bloods have godlike powers. Children of Hematoi and mortals--well, not so much. Half-bloods only have two options: become trained Sentinels who hunt and kill daimons or become servants in the homes of the pures. Seventeen-year-old Alexandria would rather risk her life fighting than waste it scrubbing toilets, but she may end up slumming it anyway. There are several rules that students at the Covenant must follow. Alex has problems with them all, but especially rule #1: Relationships between pures and halfs are forbidden. Unfortunately, she's crushing hard on the totally hot pure-blood Aiden. But falling for Aiden isn't her biggest problem--staying alive long enough to graduate the Covenant and become a Sentinel is. If she fails in her duty, she faces a future worse than death or slavery: being turned into a daimon, and being hunted by Aiden. And that would kind of suck.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435721960ra/15373540.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s been a while, my friends and since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18809475.The_Return__Titan___1_" title="The Return (Titan, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">The Return</a> I’ve been meaning to reread The Covenant series and that time has finally come.<br>It’s not a secret I love Jennifer’s writing and coming back to one of the first books I ever read by her, well, it’s awesome. She’s grown so much as a writer and it’s such a great thing to see.<br><br>Anyhow, I really loved this series and these books just get better and better, <u>that I can guarantee.</u><br><br>Let’s start with our lovely and fierce heroine, Alexandria <i>Alex</i> Andros.<br>She’s just awesome, alright?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435721960ra/15373541.gif" width="500" height="189" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love how selfless she is, she’s the kind of person who I’d love to be friends with. Or be. Or be with. I can’t quite decide. She’s <i>that</i> good.<br>At the beginning of the book we see how she’s thrown back to the Covenant and how she had to work her ass off in order to keep up with what she missed while being away her training. I loved how Aiden beat her ass, truly. I loved how bruised she was and never complained because 1). It showed how serious she was and 2). It showed how things are for halfs.<br><br>I think that, for a character who is very impulsive, she’s not that reckless and stupid.<br><br>Don’t get me wrong, she has some stupid reactions to some things but they’re not that many which is great. I also liked how friendly she is and funny. I feel like she would be such a healthy teenager given a totally different scenario, you know, someone to look up to.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430526028ra/14724974.gif" width="300" height="196" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She grows up so much in one single book and she gets more serious but that doesn’t mean she stops being this cool girl. I just like seeing things through Alex’s eyes.<br><br>Now, Aiden.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428717287ra/14474243.gif" width="245" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aiden St. Delphi, there’s a man I’m sure I’d spend the rest of my life with.<br>He’s just such a sincere guy. He’s honest, strong, fucking adorable, sexy and smart and arg!!! He gets me so frustrated because I want a man like him. Damn him.<br><br>I like how we see him getting fond of Alex day by day and how their relationship grows till the point you can feel it between the pages.<br>Aiden is such a tormented soul who had to grow up way too fast to take care of his brother after his parents were killed by daimons and he’s such a badass sentinel I just want to hug the crap out of him and then fuck him senseless, what can I say.<br><br>Girls, he’s a <i>good boy</i>, he truly is but oh, he can behave badly when he wants to. Can I get one of him for Christmas this year?<br><br>Anyways, they make a really great couple and you just have no doubt they belong together, you feel me? You feel like they could be this lovely couple doing cute couple things and having hot, hard sex and then make sweet love during the day… and then go hunting and killing things at night. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435722695ra/15373576.gif" width="500" height="223" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>Relationship goals</b>
</u><br><br>Let me tell you how much I love Caleb, please.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430526028ra/14724973.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love that man with all my heart. He’s a really great friend and <s>he deserved more</s>.<br><br>Overall I liked the friendship factor in the book, I liked pretty much all the characters, <i>even the characters I hated because they all have a purpose in the end, yeah?</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435721960ra/15373542.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, ugh, Seth. <br><br>Darling, you know I love you but you’re such a pompous asshole in this book I can’t tell you how much I wanted to maim you. I know you’ll come a long way and all that shit but still and maybe I’m getting a bit ahead of what’s gonna happen with him but yeah, asshole.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435721960ra/15373543.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and one thing I didn’t like about the book was that I couldn’t feel Alex’s loss when it came to her mother. I mean, I didn’t feel <i>that</i> when thing went south just because I didn’t know the woman and even though Alex loved her very much and it was clear she cared deeply for her daughter, I did not see it. I don’t think there were any flashbacks or moments that could lead me to care for Rachelle. I wish I had, though but since it didn’t happen, I don’t particularly care about her being dead whatsoever.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421605506ra/13391506.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, I know there are some similarities between this book and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18660669.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a>, I know.<br><br>The Academy/Covenant structure, the way half and damphir are created, the whole races structure, daimon/strogoi and some other things. And if you read this series before you read <i>Vampire Academy</i> then you’d think it’s the other way around, yeah?<br><br>Guys, yes, there are similarities but don’t let them keep you from enjoying these books. I read <i>The Covenant</i> after I read <i>Vampire Academy</i> and I’m so glad I didn’t give up on this. I think all the comparisons go away after book two. I mean, great characters, awesome characters development, badassery going on, amazing greek factor and swoon-worthy moments. I’m sold, I don’t know about you. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412240300ra/11343506.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I realised how spoiler-free are my reviews these days. Is it weird? I find it weird, LOL.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9298698573900614186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223902305?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223902305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2085097954613624543"><b>More VA similarities come out</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236492914' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372001970' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>. And that's not even my entire list of similarities. I just got tired of marking them all (because there were so many) when it started getting down to them both having rose necklaces as a significant thing and other random little details sprinkled throughout just about everywhere.<br/><br/><b>*edit* July 2012*.</b> Sigh. Eff it. I really didn't want to have a star rating on this book because of my mixed feelings (good and bad) but since I'm not risking having yet anoth</span>
  <span id="freeText2085097954613624543" style="display:none"><b>More VA similarities come out</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236492914" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372001970" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. And that's not even my entire list of similarities. I just got tired of marking them all (because there were so many) when it started getting down to them both having rose necklaces as a significant thing and other random little details sprinkled throughout just about everywhere.<br /><br /><b>*edit* July 2012*.</b> Sigh. Eff it. I really didn't want to have a star rating on this book because of my mixed feelings (good and bad) but since I'm not risking having yet another review sent to the void, I will award a star rating. <br /><br /><b>*edit* March 2012.</b> I have since removed my star rating because I don't know the fair way to rate this book anymore. If you've read <i>either</i> Half-Blood or Vampire Academy (it doesn't matter which one) this review will basically be spoiler free because you'll know what's going on from reading either book when I do my comparison. If you haven't read VA, then I'd suggest skipping this review altogether and picking up a copy of Vampire Academy. Do yourself a favor and read the original before deciding whether or not to read this. It's the only fair thing to do. Mead deserves credit for creating this world.<br /><br /><b>*edit* January 2012.</b> After having three different discussions about this book in the past few days, I'm tempted to erase my entire review. I wrote it with hope that there must have been a reason for the similarities. Now, I'm pretty sure that the author isn't claiming this as fan fic, when that's what it reads as. I tried to see the positives. I really did. <br /><br /><b>~ Original Review from 2011 ~</b><br /><br />This has got to be fan fic?<br /><br />I can't imagine that someone would blatantly rip-off the entire premise of Vampire Academy without it being some form of fan fiction. I would say at least 85% of the story was ripped from VA books 1 and 4, and the other 15% was given a Percy Jackson-like twist.<br /><br />I read the book because I was craving a Mead fix, and missing Dimitri something fierce. And this book delivered on that at least! Actually, I forgot after a while that we were dealing with offspring of the gods because when you have races like pures (moroi), half-bloods (dhampir), and daimons (strigoi), as well as jobs like sentinel (guardian), servant (blood whore), and lazy upper class (royals), all taking place on a remote island school (remote vampire academy), it's easy to forget that we're NOT reading VA. Did I mention that there is a Rose, a Dimitri (right down to being the guardian/sentinel trainer), an Eddie, a Mia and a semi-ish Adrian character? Okay, well there you go. It's VA. Did I also mention that there was a crazy <s>strigoi</s> daimon hunting our lead female? Yep. Crazy, I know.<br /><br />*edit* to also add that there were similarities between Alex/Aiden's scene and the lust charm scene in VA 1, as well as Rose/Alex wanting to train with real weapons instead of fake. I'm going to stop now before I start thinking of every single scene that was similar.<br /><br />BUT...I actually liked the story. I was engaged the entire time and never bored once. However, I'm not sure if this was because I already knew what was going on, so I didn't have to learn anything about the world, making it easier to get into right away. Heck, I may have even liked it a little bit better than VA book 1 (blasphemy, I know, especially considering how much of a Mead fangirl I am) because a lot of the world building was pushed back in favor of more action. If I was rating this book based on story alone, I'd easily go 4 stars because I enjoyed it that much. However, since there was nothing NEW about the story (oh wait, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the two Apollyons twist...hah <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), I can't in good conscience go that high. So I'm thinking 1 star for originality. Not even one thing about the mythology was new. I'd read it all before in other books, and some of it felt like I was rehashing Percy Jackson (especially the part with the oracle).<br /><br />So uh...yeah. I really liked the book! I can't wait to read the next one! Let's hope it branches off into something completely different so I can go higher on the rating because I really did like the author's <s>storytelling</s>, <s>fresh characters</s> errr...writing style. Yeah, that!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2085097954613624543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1952461828624513736" style="display:none"><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/funny%20gif/girly-girl-graphics/animation/1504-09-24-2011.gif?o=31" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384874ra/743562.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/happy%20gifs/princessaili/gif%20macros/tumblr_m4lxxoss5d1rn3yoz.gif?o=39" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380351192ra/704887.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/happy%20gifs/ChristineFerrara/GIFs/HappyDance.gif?o=128" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/happy%20gifs/gjhm2/Mood%20gifs/jadsleld.gif?o=141" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <span>[image error]</span>
</a><br>Yes! I am extremely happy!<br>This book exceeded my expectations!<br><br><br><b>THE GIST</b><br><br>Here are some of the things you need to know about first before I get to the real gist of this book. We all know that the Greek gods were very fond of mingling with humans. And when they mingle with humans in a not so innocent way, the by-products would be the Half-bloods. But of course there was another type of Hematoi (children of the gods) and they were the Pures who were the offsprings of two Pures which basically means both of them are descendants of gods. The Pures were considered as the upper class citizens while the Half-bloods were the second to lower class citizens. There was no equality between the two. The pure-bloods were given all the privileges while the half-bloods either become Sentinels or become slaves of the Pures (talk about discrimination huh?). Union between the Half-bloods and the Pures were also forbidden.<br><br>So here is the real gist! <br><br>Alexandria Andros was a half-blood. She was the daughter of a pure and a human. When she was thirteen her mother ran away from the Covenant (Hematoi school) for a reason her mother never explained to her. Three years have passed their worst fear came, the Daimons found them. Alex was able to escape but horror filled her because she saw her mother killed before her very eyes by the Daimons. Fortunately, people from the Covenant a Pure named Aiden St. Delphi (the guy she’s been secretly fantasizing over for three years) found Alex and took her back to where she belongs. But does she really belong there? Why did her mother discreetly took her away from that place? What was the secret? Will she ever find out? Will her attraction to Aiden cause her troubles? How will she deal with her mother’s death?<br><br>The answers to those would shock the hell out of you!! <br><br><br><b>FIRST IMPRESSION</b><br><br>This book actually proved to me that first impressions are not always right. This book sucker punched me with its awesomeness!<br><br>But okay to be honest my first impression on this book was not good. I read Daimon first because I was told by my friend who recommended this series to read it first and I did. Problem was at that time I wasn’t sure why but the book didn’t give me anything. It didn’t give me the same fired up feeling that I got when I read it the second time. After Daimon, I immediately went and read Half-Blood which gave me ecstatic feeling although out reading this book!<br><br>Why did I reread it? Well basically because Daemon from Obsidian made me do it! :p You guys get what I mean!<br><br>Yep! First impressions does not last for long especially if there is an Aiden St. Delphi to make you change your mind!<br><br><br><b>CHARACTERS</b><br><br>There are a lot of seriously amazing characters here. Of course there’s <s>Aiden</s> Alex.<br><br>Alex was definitely my type of girl. She may not be a Pure but she is one hell of a fighter. She was kickass! She was also annoying at times because she has no regard for the rules but even though it’s annoying I still like her. Why? Because she wasn’t the typical goody goody female lead. I hate weak female lead. She does get her ass kicked a lot but still she was definitely a character you’ll love! She was strong. She was outspoken up to the point that sometimes for me it was totally disrespectful already (one thing I didn’t like about her). <br><br>I didn’t know what to expect with the male lead character Aiden. I mean yeah Daemon from Obsidian was hot as hell but I didn’t know that Jennifer could create someone as hot as Daemon but in a different way! Ohhh Jennifer! I’d like to know if you have Daemons and Aiden’s hanging out with you there because I want to have one!! Aheeemm. Back to talking about Aiden! Let me just make it short. There is nothing you wouldn’t like about Aiden. He was the perfect gentleman. He was nice even though he was a Pure. He was gorgeous. He was body was chiselled in all the right places. He was totally <s>delicious</s> a total hottie.<br><br>Seth was someone I didn’t see coming. Yeah he was the type of guy who you’d like to kick in the groin for being so arrogant! But yeah he has this soft spot too that I didn’t expect to be there. Hope to get more out of him on the next books! And I hope he doesn’t turn out bad because I’d be heartbroken. Oh yeah! Seth is <s>delicious</s> a hottie too just so you guys know!<br><br>The supporting characters were there to love and hate too. I love Alex’s friend Caleb. He was a total sweetheart. Leah was a totally <s>Btch!</s> hateful. Marcus (Alex’s uncle) and Lucien (Alex’s stepdad) all played their roles well. <br><br><br><b>ALEX + AIDEN = MATCH MADE IN HEAVEN</b><br><br>ALEX and AIDEN was a match made in heaven!<br>If I was to rate this book just based on their chemistry, I would have given this book an immediate 5!<br>The thing between them was undeniable even without them saying anything about it.<br>All that pent up tension!!! <br>Waaaaahhhh! I couldn’t take it!<br>I want more ALEX and AIDEN!<br><br><br><b>QUOTABLE QUOTES</b><br><br><i>“Two people see each across a room or their skin brushes. Their souls recognize the person as their own. It doesn’t need time to figure it. The soul always knows… whether it’s right or wrong.”</i><br><br><i>“People do the damndest things when they’re in love.” </i><br><br><i>“I was gonna be super pissed in the afterlife if I died a virgin in this crap hole.” </i><br><br><br><b>HIGHLIGHTS</b><br><br>If you are looking for highlights there are a lot but let me just list my faves:<br><br>* I am a fan of Greek Myth so it’s pretty important to me that it is used in a way that it won’t be disrespectful to how the Greeks made their gods to be. I am proud to say that this book did not mess it up. Ms. Armentrout just used it and made it relatable to the current times. <br><br>* The characters were well developed for me. Kickass female lead and a swoon worthy male lead! What more could you ask for?<br><br>* Oh my gods! I love the pace and how the story developed. Usually fast paced books have fewer details on the lives of the characters but this one just had the right amount of information and action.<br><br>* The chemistry was out of this world! Alex and Aiden are two characters definitely to watch out for.<br><br> <br><b>FINAL WORDS</b><br><br>Okay so I have read loads of reviews comparing this book to Vampire Academy. Honestly, I wouldn’t know because I haven’t read that yet. But one this for sure, I still would love the Covenant series. Whether I read VA or not, whether or not it’s the same or not, I don’t freakin’ care. <br><br>All readers are different. Some interpret things the way they want it to become. Readers have to keep an open mind though that sometimes it may really be just coincidental but really it’s wrong to judge that they plagiarized someone’s work. That is just so wrong. Respect people!<br><br>Anyhow, I would definitely be recommending this book especially for those who love mythology like me and for those who want a good paranormal romance novel! It totally exceeded my expectation. It has everything that I could ever ask for in a book plus a lot of add-ons on the side. <br><br><b>Ms. Jennifer Armentrout, you did it again! </b><br>You made me squeal in anticipation for your next books!<br><br><br>A very happy group of minions for this book!<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/happy%20gifs/sicsempertyrannosaurusrex/Reaction%20GIFs/HappythingsfromDespicableMe.gif?o=3" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <span>[image error]</span>
</a><br><br><b>5 stars!</b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471107805?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471107805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5392763387402930303"><br/>Every once in a while a reader might be fortunate enough to stumble upon a piece of published literature that makes them feel <b> SO BLOOD ADEQUATE </b> as an aspiring author.<br/><br/>For me, this book has done it. <br/><br/>If this stuff can be published and loved then I think I’m gonna be a best-selling author in multiple universes. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487631035ra/22034042.gif' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Name your most hated clichéd tropes, kids and I will guarantee you will find them in this book. :)<br/><br/> 1.	The writing is so immature. IT’S LIKE A TEN YEAR OLD WAS GIVEN A FREE PASS AT WRITING F</span>
  <span id="freeText5392763387402930303" style="display:none"><br>Every once in a while a reader might be fortunate enough to stumble upon a piece of published literature that makes them feel <b> SO BLOOD ADEQUATE </b> as an aspiring author.<br><br>For me, this book has done it. <br><br>If this stuff can be published and loved then I think I’m gonna be a best-selling author in multiple universes. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487631035ra/22034042.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Name your most hated clichéd tropes, kids and I will guarantee you will find them in this book. :)<br><br> 1.	The writing is so immature. IT’S LIKE A TEN YEAR OLD WAS GIVEN A FREE PASS AT WRITING FAN FICTION AND THIS IS THE BEST THEY CAME UP WITH.<br><br> 2.	If someone could direct me to the plot that would be great, still trying to figure out what the purpose of the book is. . . <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450516197ra/17438605.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> 3.	//AIDAN IS HOT. HE’S REALLY SUPER HOT. He’s probably as hot as the sun. No, maybe hotter. Did you catch that one, guys? He’s hot. GORGEOUSLY HOT//<br><br><i> "The grin increased to a full smile. And… oh, man. He had dimples. The air in my lungs died." </i> <br><br><i> "Aiden was… hotness incarnate. I alternated between staring at those ripped arms and being envious of how he moved with such fluid grace, but it was more than just his ability to make me drool on myself." </i><br><br>Please, stop. <br><br> 4.	OH MY GOD, WHO WOULD LIKE <b>ME</b>??? I’M SO UGLY WITH MY PLATIUM HAIR AND MY PERFECTLY TONED AND SCUPLTED BODY AND CHISELED FEATURES LIKE EW, I’M SO UGLY. <br><br><i> "I’d been so stunningly beautiful he couldn’t help but notice me. That last one was the most absurd. I’d been gawky and a total dweeb then" </i><br><br>Someone end me.<br><br>5.	Oh and there’s <i> Girl Hate™ </i> bc no book is successful without a little bit of Girl Hate™.<br><br><i> "Lea sauntered in, and I swear, she managed to get the uniform as tight as humanly possible. I looked down at my own and noted that my legs looked nowhere near as good as hers did. Bitch." </i><br><br>6.	Everything is so . . .dramatic !!! yet not interesting enough for me to CARE why it’s so dramatic.<br><br>7.	I have no idea what the ending is. My brain went into Protection Mode and saved me the trauma of having to remember the final chapter. <br><br><br>Overall, this book was a wonder!!! :) :) :)<br><br><br>1 star!!<br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><i> <b> Buddy read </b> with my girl, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/60226508-blue" rel="nofollow noopener">Bluey</a> </i> ~ thanks for BRing this with mehhhh &lt;3 &lt;3 <br><br><br></span>
